Everything is working. Here's the status:  

**Server running at http://localhost:23000** on `feature/team-governance` branch with all governance features:  

- **Governance API**: `/api/governance` — returns password/manager state  
- **Teams API**: `/api/teams` — CRUD with ACL guards, closed team support  
- **Transfer API**: `/api/governance/transfers` — transfer requests for closed teams  
- **Skills installed**: Both `agent-messaging` (with governance section) and `team-governance` skills updated at 17:30  

**What to test in the browser:**  

1. **Open an agent profile** — you should see a `+ Assign Role` badge in the header  
2. **Click `+ Assign Role`** — opens the role assignment dialog (MANAGER, Chief-of-Staff, Normal)  
3. **Select MANAGER** and confirm — triggers the password setup dialog (first time)  
4. **Set a governance password** (min 6 chars) — assigns the MANAGER role  
5. **Check another agent** — should show "Warning: current manager is X" if you try to assign MANAGER again  
6. **Create a team** on the `/teams` page — set type to "closed"  
7. **Assign Chief-of-Staff** to a closed team via agent profile  
8. **Team Membership section** — replaces the old free-text Team field, shows join/leave controls  
9. **Message Center** — autocomplete should filter unreachable agents in closed teams  

Your tmux sessions and agents are completely untouched — I only restarted the web server process.

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 17:35:08]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Bash -- Create PR via gh CLI</summary>

**Input:**

*Create PR via gh CLI*  

```bash
gh pr create \
  --repo 23blocks-OS/ai-maestro \
  --head Emasoft:feature/team-governance \
  --base main \
  --title "Add team governance: closed teams, roles, messaging isolation, transfers (v0.23.10)" \
  --body "$(cat <<'EOF'
## Summary

Adds a complete team governance system with role-based access control, messaging isolation for closed teams, and a transfer approval workflow.

- **Closed teams**: Teams can be set to `open` (default) or `closed` type. Closed teams enforce messaging isolation — members can only message within their team
- **MANAGER role**: Global singleton with full authority over all teams and messaging
- **Chief-of-Staff (COS) role**: Per-team leader for closed teams, acts as the bridge between inside and outside the team
- **Messaging filter**: Enforces governance rules on all messages (AMP and UI) — blocks cross-team messages for closed teams
- **Transfer requests**: Workflow to move agents between closed teams with approval from source COS or MANAGER
- **Governance UI**: Role badges, password-protected role assignment dialogs, team membership section, filtered message recipients
- **ACL guards**: Team API routes enforce governance rules (only COS/MANAGER can modify closed teams)
- **File locking**: In-process mutex for team-registry, governance, and transfer-registry writes
- **297 tests passing** including new governance and transfer-registry test suites

## New Files (19)

| File | Purpose |
|------|---------|
| `lib/governance.ts` | Governance state: password hashing, MANAGER/COS role management |
| `lib/message-filter.ts` | Message reachability rules for closed team isolation |
| `lib/transfer-registry.ts` | Transfer request CRUD with file-based persistence |
| `lib/team-acl.ts` | ACL helpers for team route authorization |
| `lib/file-lock.ts` | In-process Map-based mutex with `withLock` |
| `types/governance.ts` | SSOT types for governance config, transfer requests |
| `app/api/governance/route.ts` | GET

... [2797 more chars truncated]

**Result:**

Loading .zprofile at 17:35:08  
https://github.com/23blocks-OS/ai-maestro/pull/229

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 17:38:35]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FFC107; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Here's what `update-aimaestro.sh` does:  

1. **Checks for uncommitted changes** — auto-stashes with `-y` flag (line 127-141)  
2. **Fetches from `origin main`** — `git fetch origin main` (line 149)  
3. **Compares HEAD to `origin/main`** — counts commits behind (line 151)  
4. **If behind**: pulls `origin main` with `git pull origin main` (line 187)  
5. **If already up-to-date**: asks to reinstall scripts/skills anyway (auto-yes with `-y`)  
6. **Installs dependencies**: `yarn install` (line 197)  
7. **Builds**: `yarn build` (line 206)  
8. **Reinstalls tools** via component installers:  
   - `install-messaging.sh -y` — AMP scripts + skills  
   - `install-memory-tools.sh -y`  
   - `install-graph-tools.sh -y`  
   - `install-doc-tools.sh -y`  
   - `install-agent-cli.sh -y`  
   - `scripts/claude-hooks/install-hooks.sh -y`  
9. **Runs verification**: `verify-installation.sh`  
10. **Restarts PM2**: `pm2 restart ai-maestro`  

The key thing: on line 149 it does `git fetch origin main` and on line 187 `git pull origin main`. Since we're on `feature/team-governance` and that branch is ahead of `origin/main` (not behind), the script reported "You're already on the latest version!" and didn't pull. It just reinstalled scripts/skills and rebuilt — which is why our governance code stayed intact. No branch switch happened.  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 17:42:35]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FFC107; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Here's the difference:  

**`pm2 start ecosystem.config.js`** — First-time registration. Reads the config file, registers the process with PM2 using all the settings (name, script, env vars, log paths, memory limits, restart policies), and starts it. If the process is already registered, it starts a **new instance** (which can cause duplicates).  

**`pm2 restart ai-maestro`** — Restarts an already-registered process by name. Uses whatever config PM2 already has in memory. Does not re-read `ecosystem.config.js`.  

The updater uses `pm2 restart ai-maestro` because it assumes AI Maestro was already registered with PM2 from a previous `pm2 start ecosystem.config.js`. This is the correct call for an update — you're restarting the existing process, not registering a new one.  

**When to use which:**  

| Command | Use when |  
|---------|----------|  
| `pm2 start ecosystem.config.js` | First install, or after `pm2 delete ai-maestro` |  
| `pm2 restart ai-maestro` | After code updates, rebuilds (process already registered) |  

If you change `ecosystem.config.js` itself (e.g. env vars, memory limits), you'd need `pm2 delete ai-maestro` then `pm2 start ecosystem.config.js` to pick up the new config — `restart` won't re-read it.  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 17:46:12]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FFC107; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">



Yes, exactly. So there are actually three cases:  

| Command | Use when |  
|---------|----------|  
| `pm2 start ecosystem.config.js` | First install, or after `pm2 delete ai-maestro` |  
| `pm2 restart ai-maestro` | Code/build changes only (config unchanged) |  
| `pm2 delete ai-maestro && pm2 start ecosystem.config.js` | `ecosystem.config.js` itself was changed |  

The updater script currently only handles case 2. If a future PR changes `ecosystem.config.js` (env vars, memory limits, script path, log paths, etc.), `pm2 restart ai-maestro` would silently keep the old config in memory. The updater should detect that case and do a delete+start instead.  

Want me to open a GitHub issue to track this as a future improvement to `update-aimaestro.sh`?  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 17:51:20]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FFC107; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Good point — `pm2 restart ecosystem.config.js` re-reads the config and restarts, which is the correct migration path. So the logic in the updater should be:  

1. Check if `ecosystem.config.js` changed in the update (`git diff` before/after pull)  
2. If changed: exit with an error telling the user to run `pm2 restart ecosystem.config.js`  
3. If unchanged: proceed with `pm2 restart ai-maestro` as usual  

</div>


## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 17:51:30]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Bash -- Create GitHub issue for updater config detection</summary>

**Input:**

*Create GitHub issue for updater config detection*  

```bash
gh issue create \
  --repo 23blocks-OS/ai-maestro \
  --title "update-aimaestro.sh: detect ecosystem.config.js changes and require pm2 restart ecosystem.config.js" \
  --label "enhancement" \
  --body "$(cat <<'EOF'
## Problem

The updater script (`update-aimaestro.sh`) always runs `pm2 restart ai-maestro` after pulling changes. This only restarts the process using PM2's cached config — it does NOT re-read `ecosystem.config.js`.

If a release changes `ecosystem.config.js` (env vars, memory limits, script path, log paths, etc.), `pm2 restart ai-maestro` silently keeps the old config, which can cause subtle runtime issues.

## Expected Behavior

After `git pull`, the updater should:

1. Check if `ecosystem.config.js` was modified in the pulled commits
2. If **unchanged**: proceed with `pm2 restart ai-maestro` (current behavior)
3. If **changed**: stop and print an error message like:

```
ERROR: ecosystem.config.js has changed in this update.  
PM2 needs to reload the configuration.  

Run this command to apply the new config:  
  pm2 restart ecosystem.config.js  

Then re-run: ./update-aimaestro.sh  
```

## Implementation Notes

Detection can be done with:
```bash
BEFORE_SHA=$(git rev-parse HEAD)  
git pull origin main  
if ! git diff --quiet "$BEFORE_SHA" HEAD -- ecosystem.config.js; then  
  # config changed — require pm2 restart ecosystem.config.js  
fi  
```

Three PM2 commands and when to use each:

| Command | Reads config? | Use when |
|---------|--------------|----------|
| `pm2 start ecosystem.config.js` | Yes | First install |
| `pm2 restart ai-maestro` | No | Code changes only |
| `pm2 restart ecosystem.config.js` | Yes | Config changed |
EOF
)"
```

**Result:**

Loading .zprofile at 17:51:30  
https://github.com/23blocks-OS/ai-maestro/issues/230  

</details>

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 17:52:25]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FFC107; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">



`pm2 restart ai-maestro` — Restarts the process by name using the config PM2 cached in memory when it was first started. Any changes to `ecosystem.config.js` on disk are ignored.  

`pm2 restart ecosystem.config.js` — Reads `ecosystem.config.js` from disk, then restarts the process with the updated config (new env vars, memory limits, log paths, etc.).  

Same restart action, but one uses stale cached config and the other re-reads from the file.  

</div>

     7→  const teams = loadTeams()  
     8→  return NextResponse.json({ teams })  
     9→}  
    10→  
    11→// POST /api/teams - Create a new team  
    12→export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
    13→  try {  
    14→    const body = await request.json()  
    15→    const { name, description, agentIds, type, chiefOfStaffId } = body  
    16→  
    17→    if (!name || typeof name !== 'string') {  
    18→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Team name is required' }, { status: 400 })  
    19→    }  
    20→  
    21→    if (agentIds && !Array.isArray(agentIds)) {  
    22→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'agentIds must be an array' }, { status: 400 })  
    23→    }  
    24→  
    25→    const team = await createTeam({ name, description, agentIds: agentIds || [], type, chiefOfStaffId })  
    26→    return NextResponse.json({ team }, { status: 201 })  
    27→  } catch (error) {  
    28→    console.error('Failed to create team:', error)  
    29→    return NextResponse.json(  
    30→      { error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Failed to create team' },  
    31→      { status: 500 }  
    32→    )  
    33→  }  
    34→}

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 18:09:11]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `team-acl.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

```json
{
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/team-acl.ts"
}
```

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * Team Resource ACL — checks whether an agent (or web UI request)  
     3→ * is allowed to access a given team's resources.  
     4→ *  
     5→ * Open teams (type undefined or 'open') impose no restrictions.  
     6→ * Closed teams restrict access to the manager, chief-of-staff,  
     7→ * and team members only.  
     8→ */  
     9→  
    10→import { isManager } from './governance'  
    11→import { getTeam } from './team-registry'  
    12→  
    13→export interface TeamAccessInput {  
    14→  teamId: string  
    15→  requestingAgentId?: string // undefined = web UI request (always allowed)  
    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface TeamAccessResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Determine whether the requester may access the team's resources.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Decision order:  
    27→ *  1. Web UI (no agentId)      → allowed  
    28→ *  2. Team not found           → allowed (caller handles 404)  
    29→ *  3. Team is open / untyped   → allowed  
    30→ *  4. Requester is MANAGER     → allowed  
    31→ *  5. Requester is chief-of-staff → allowed  
    32→ *  6. Requester is a member    → allowed  
    33→ *  7. Otherwise                → denied  
    34→ */  
    35→export function checkTeamAccess(input: TeamAccessInput): TeamAccessResult {  
    36→  // 1. Web UI requests (no X-Agent-Id header) always pass  
    37→  if (input.requestingAgentId === undefined) {  
    38→    return { allowed: true }  
    39→  }  
    40→  
    41→  // 2. Team not found — let the caller deal with 404  
    42→  const team = getTeam(input.teamId)  
    43→  if (!team) {  
    44→    return { allowed: true }  
    45→  }  
    46→  
    47→  // 3. Open teams (or teams with no explicit type) have no ACL  
    48→  if (team.type !== 'closed') {  
    49→    return { allowed: true }  
    50→  }  
    51→  
    52→  // 4. MANAGER role always has access  
    53→  if (isManager(input.requestingAgentId)) {  
    54→    return { allowed: true }  
    55→  }  
    56→  
    57→  // 5.   

... [474 more chars truncated]  

</details>

     6→interface UseTeamResult {

     8→  loading: boolean

    13→  
    14→export function useTeam(teamId: string | null): UseTeamResult {  
    15→  const [team, setTeam] = useState<Team | null>(null)  
    16→  const [loading, setLoading] = useState(false)  
    17→  const [error, setError] = useState<string | null>(null)  
    18→  
    19→  const fetchTeam = useCallback(async () => {  
    20→    if (!teamId) return  
    21→    try {  
    22→      const res = await fetch(`/api/teams/${teamId}`)  
    23→      if (!res.ok) throw new Error('Failed to fetch team')  
    24→      const data = await res.json()  
    25→      setTeam(data.team || null)  
    26→      setError(null)  
    27→    } catch (err) {  
    28→      setError(err instanceof Error ? err.message : 'Failed to fetch team')  
    29→    }  
    30→  }, [teamId])  
    31→  
    32→  // Initial fetch  
    33→  useEffect(() => {  
    34→    if (!teamId) {  
    35→      setTeam(null)  
    36→      return  
    37→    }  
    38→    setLoading(true)  
    39→    fetchTeam().finally(() => setLoading(false))  
    40→  }, [teamId, fetchTeam])  
    41→  
    42→  const updateTeam = useCallback(async (updates: { name?: string; description?: string; agentIds?: string[]; instructions?: string }) => {  
    43→    if (!teamId) return  
    44→    // Optimistic update

    13→/**  
    14→ * Check if a host URL points to localhost (the machine running this dashboard)  
    15→ * Used client-side since os.hostname() isn't available in browser

    17→function isLocalhostUrl(url: string | undefined): boolean {

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 18:10:47]*


## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 18:10:52]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FFC107; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

I found the root causes. Here's what's going on:  

**Issue 2 — "Team section asks to authenticate"**: Can you clarify what you saw exactly? The code doesn't have authentication on the teams page. Was it a password dialog, a 403 error, or something else? The ACL in `team-acl.ts:37-39` explicitly allows all web UI requests (no `X-Agent-Id` header = always allowed).  

**Issue 3 — "Create button does nothing, then creates after 1-2 minutes"**: Found the bug. In `app/teams/page.tsx:60-80`, `handleCreateTeam` is async but the button has **no loading state** — it stays clickable during the API call. Each click fires a new POST. Since `createTeam` uses `withLock`, all requests serialize (one after another). That's why you got 7 duplicate teams:  

```
{"teams":[
  {"name":"pinosan-manager"}, {"name":"pinosan-manager"}, {"name":"pinosan-manager"},
  {"name":"pinosan5"}, {"name":"pinosan5"},
  {"name":"yyytplmnjiuhb"}, {"name":"yt"}
]}
```

You clicked many times, nothing seemed to happen, then `router.push` fired after the last one completed.  

**Issue 4 — "Agent list empty when assigning"**: In `app/teams/[id]/page.tsx:31`, the loading spinner only checks `useTeam` loading, not `useAgents` loading. If the team loads before agents finish fetching, `TeamOverviewSection` renders with `agents=[]`, showing "No available agents to add".  

Shall I fix these 3 bugs now?  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 18:17:02]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `page.tsx`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/teams/page.tsx`  

**Old:**  
```
  const handleCreateTeam = async () => {
    if (!newTeamName.trim()) return
    try {
      const res = await fetch('/api/teams', {
        method: 'POST',
        headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },
        body: JSON.stringify({ name: newTeamName.trim(), agentIds: [] }),
      })
      if (!res.ok) {
        const errData = await res.json()
        throw new Error(errData.error || 'Failed to create team')
      }
      const data = await res.json()
      setNewTeamName('')
      setCreating(false)
      // Navigate to the new team
      router.push(`/teams/${data.team.id}`)
    } catch (err) {
      console.error('Failed to create team:', err)
    }
  }
```

**New:**  
```
  const handleCreateTeam = async () => {
    if (!newTeamName.trim() || submitting) return
    setSubmitting(true)
    setCreateError(null)
    try {
      const res = await fetch('/api/teams', {
        method: 'POST',
        headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },
        body: JSON.stringify({ name: newTeamName.trim(), agentIds: [] }),
      })
      if (!res.ok) {
        const errData = await res.json()
        throw new Error(errData.error || 'Failed to create team')
      }
      const data = await res.json()
      setNewTeamName('')
      setCreating(false)
      router.push(`/teams/${data.team.id}`)
    } catch (err) {
      const msg = err instanceof Error ? err.message : 'Failed to create team'
      setCreateError(msg)
      console.error('Failed to create team:', err)
    } finally {
      setSubmitting(false)
    }
  }
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/teams/page.tsx has been updated successfully.

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 18:17:17]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `page.tsx`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/teams/page.tsx`  

**Old:**  
```
      {/* Create Team Dialog */}
      {creating && (
        <div className="fixed inset-0 z-50 flex items-center justify-center bg-black/60 backdrop-blur-sm">
          <div className="bg-gray-900 border border-gray-700 rounded-xl p-6 max-w-sm w-full mx-4">
            <h4 className="text-sm font-medium text-white mb-4">Create Team</h4>
            <input
              type="text"
              value={newTeamName}
              onChange={e => setNewTeamName(e.target.value)}
              placeholder="Team name..."
              className="w-full bg-gray-800 border border-gray-700 rounded-lg px-3 py-2 text-sm text-white focus:outline-none focus:border-emerald-500 mb-4"
              autoFocus
              onKeyDown={e => { if (e.key === 'Enter') handleCreateTeam(); if (e.key === 'Escape') setCreating(false) }}
            />
            <div className="flex justify-end gap-2">
              <button
                onClick={() => { setCreating(false); setNewTeamName('') }}
                className="text-xs px-3 py-1.5 bg-gray-700 hover:bg-gray-600 text-gray-300 rounded transition-colors"
              >
                Cancel
              </button>
              <button
                onClick={handleCreateTeam}
                disabled={!newTeamName.trim()}
                className="text-xs px-3 py-1.5 bg-emerald-600 hover:bg-emerald-700 text-white rounded transition-colors disabled:opacity-50"
              >
                Create
              </button>
            </div>
          </div>
        </div>
      )}
```

**New:**  
```
      {/* Create Team Dialog */}
      {creating && (
        <div className="fixed inset-0 z-50 flex items-center justify-center bg-black/60 backdrop-blur-sm">

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 18:18:37]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FFC107; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Both fixes are deployed. Here's what changed:  

**Issue 3 — Create Team dialog:**  
- Button is now disabled while the API call is in progress (`submitting` guard)  
- Dialog shows a spinner with "Creating team..." text while waiting  
- Input and buttons are hidden during submission (prevents double-clicks)  
- Error message appears in red if creation fails  
- Error clears when you type a new name or close the dialog  

**Issue 4 — Agent list in team overview:**  
- "Add Agent" dropdown shows a spinner with "Loading agents..." while `useAgents` is fetching  
- If agent fetch fails, shows error message with a "Retry" button  
- Team members list also shows a loading spinner while agents load  
- All loading/error states pass through from `useAgents` hook  

I also cleaned up the 7 duplicate test teams. You can test again at http://localhost:23000.  

</div>


## <span style="color:#2196F3">◆ USER</span>  *[2026-02-16 18:33:32]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

check your changes for errors, missing things, broken references, race conditions, timeouts, missing error messages, infinite loops, blocking operations, accidental creations of multiple teams, accidental multiple changes due to fadt repeated clicks, lack of error messages, handling of all edge cases and possible errors, prevention of creation of multiple teams with the same name, prevention of adding the same user multiple times to a team, enforce the choice of a chief-of-staff agent when creating a closed team. closed team cannot exist without a chief-of-staff, since he is the one responsible for the external communication and of adding/removing agents to the closed team (this is why it is called chief-of-staff.. he decides the staff composing of a team). Of course the MANAGER can do it too, but rarely does. it usually create a closed team with a chief-of-staff and let the chief-of-staff add the other agents to it, but it can also do everything by himself. A chief-of-staff can be removed from a team, but then the team is immediatly downgraded to open-team. it needs to be edited and updated to close again by a manager or by a chief-of-staff to be a closed team again. and when you change the team to closed, you MUST indicate the chief-of-staff assigned to it. Remember that managers and chief-of-staffs can be assigned to multiple closed teams at the same time. while normal agents can only be assigned to one closed team at any given time, but can be assigned to many open teams at the same time without problems. be sure both thevscripts and the ui will always report the list of teams each agent belongs to when they are choosen from a list to be added/removed/transferred to/from teams or selected to create a new team.  

</div>

     1→import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     2→import { checkMessageAllowed } from '@/lib/message-filter'  
     3→import { loadAgents } from '@/lib/agent-registry'  
     4→  
     5→// In-memory cache: avoids re-reading governance + teams files for every agent  
     6→// on each request. TTL of 5 seconds balances freshness with performance.  
     7→const cache = new Map<string, { ids: string[]; expiresAt: number }>()  
     8→const CACHE_TTL_MS = 5_000  
     9→  
    10→export async function GET(request: NextRequest) {  
    11→  try {  
    12→    const agentId = request.nextUrl.searchParams.get('agentId')  
    13→  
    14→    if (!agentId) {  
    15→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'agentId query parameter is required' }, { status: 400 })  
    16→    }  
    17→  
    18→    // Check cache first  
    19→    const cached = cache.get(agentId)  
    20→    if (cached && Date.now() < cached.expiresAt) {  
    21→      return NextResponse.json({ reachableAgentIds: cached.ids })  
    22→    }  
    23→  
    24→    // Cache miss or expired — compute reachable agents  
    25→    const allAgents = loadAgents()  
    26→    const reachableAgentIds: string[] = []  
    27→  
    28→    for (const agent of allAgents) {  
    29→      if (agent.id === agentId) continue  
    30→      if (agent.deletedAt) continue  
    31→  
    32→      const result = checkMessageAllowed({  
    33→        senderAgentId: agentId,  
    34→        recipientAgentId: agent.id,  
    35→      })  
    36→  
    37→      if (result.allowed) {  
    38→        reachableAgentIds.push(agent.id)  
    39→      }  
    40→    }  
    41→  
    42→    // Store in cache with TTL  
    43→    cache.set(agentId, { ids: reachableAgentIds, expiresAt: Date.now() + CACHE_TTL_MS })  
    44→  
    45→    // Evict stale entries to prevent unbounded growth  
    46→    if (cache.size > 200) {  
    47→      const now = Date.now()  
    48→      for (const [key, entry] of cache) {  
    49→        if (now >= entry.expiresAt) cache.delete(key)  
    50→      }  
    51  

... [286 more chars truncated]  

</details>

   100→  
   101→/**  
   102→ * Compute tmux session name from agent name and session index  
   103→ * Examples:  
   104→ *   ("website", 0) → "website"  
   105→ *   ("website", 1) → "website_1"  
   106→ *   ("23blocks-apps-backend", 0) → "23blocks-apps-backend"  
   107→ *   ("23blocks-apps-backend", 2) → "23blocks-apps-backend_2"  
   108→ */  
   109→export function computeSessionName(agentName: string, index: number): string {  
   110→  return index === 0 ? agentName : `${agentName}_${index}`  
   111→}  
   112→  
   113→/**  
   114→ * Derive display info from agent name for UI hierarchy  
   115→ * Splits on hyphens to create tags + shortName  
   116→ * Examples:  
   117→ *   "website" → { tags: [], shortName: "website" }  
   118→ *   "23blocks-apps-website" → { tags: ["23blocks", "apps"], shortName: "website" }  
   119→ */  
   120→export function parseNameForDisplay(name: string): { tags: string[]; shortName: string } {  
   121→  const segments = name.split(/-/).filter(s => s.length > 0)  
   122→  if (segments.length === 1) {  
   123→    return { tags: [], shortName: segments[0] }  
   124→  }  
   125→  return {  
   126→    tags: segments.slice(0, -1),  
   127→    shortName: segments[segments.length - 1]  
   128→  }  
   129→}  
   130→  
   131→// ============================================================================  
   132→// Agent Session (Multi-Brain Support)  
   133→// ============================================================================  
   134→  
   135→/**  
   136→ * A single session belonging to an agent  
   137→ * Agents can have multiple sessions acting as specialized "brains"  
   138→ */

     1→/**  
     2→ * Team Resource ACL — checks whether an agent (or web UI request)  
     3→ * is allowed to access a given team's resources.  
     4→ *  
     5→ * Open teams (type undefined or 'open') impose no restrictions.  
     6→ * Closed teams restrict access to the manager, chief-of-staff,  
     7→ * and team members only.  
     8→ */  
     9→  
    10→import { isManager } from './governance'  
    11→import { getTeam } from './team-registry'  
    12→  
    13→export interface TeamAccessInput {  
    14→  teamId: string  
    15→  requestingAgentId?: string // undefined = web UI request (always allowed)  
    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface TeamAccessResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Determine whether the requester may access the team's resources.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Decision order:  
    27→ *  1. Web UI (no agentId)      → allowed  
    28→ *  2. Team not found           → allowed (caller handles 404)  
    29→ *  3. Team is open / untyped   → allowed  
    30→ *  4. Requester is MANAGER     → allowed  
    31→ *  5. Requester is chief-of-staff → allowed  
    32→ *  6. Requester is a member    → allowed  
    33→ *  7. Otherwise                → denied  
    34→ */  
    35→export function checkTeamAccess(input: TeamAccessInput): TeamAccessResult {  
    36→  // 1. Web UI requests (no X-Agent-Id header) always pass  
    37→  if (input.requestingAgentId === undefined) {  
    38→    return { allowed: true }  
    39→  }  
    40→  
    41→  // 2. Team not found — let the caller deal with 404  
    42→  const team = getTeam(input.teamId)  
    43→  if (!team) {  
    44→    return { allowed: true }  
    45→  }  
    46→  
    47→  // 3. Open teams (or teams with no explicit type) have no ACL  
    48→  if (team.type !== 'closed') {  
    49→    return { allowed: true }  
    50→  }  
    51→  
    52→  // 4. MANAGER role always has access  
    53→  if (isManager(input.requestingAgentId)) {  
    54→    return { allowed: true }  
    55→  }  
    56→  
    57→  // 5.   

... [474 more chars truncated]  

</details>

     1→/**  
     2→ * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Determines whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed  
     5→ * based on governance roles (MANAGER, Chief-of-Staff) and closed-team  
     6→ * membership. Open-world agents (not in any closed team) can message  
     7→ * freely unless the recipient is inside a closed team.  
     8→ */  
     9→  
    10→import { isManager, isChiefOfStaffAnywhere, getClosedTeamForAgent } from './governance'  
    11→  
    12→export interface MessageFilterInput {  
    13→  senderAgentId: string | null // null = mesh-forwarded message  
    14→  recipientAgentId: string  
    15→  isMeshForwarded?: boolean  
    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface MessageFilterResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Check whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Algorithm:  
    27→ * 1. Mesh-forwarded (senderAgentId null): always allowed (trust mesh peers)  
    28→ * 2. Neither in a closed team: allowed (open world, current behavior)  
    29→ * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed  
    30→ * 4. Sender is COS of any closed team: can reach MANAGER, other COS, own team members  
    31→ * 5. Normal closed-team member: can reach same-team members and own COS  
    32→ * 6. Outside sender to closed-team recipient: denied  
    33→ * 7. Default: allowed  
    34→ */  
    35→export function checkMessageAllowed(input: MessageFilterInput): MessageFilterResult {  
    36→  const { senderAgentId, recipientAgentId } = input  
    37→  
    38→  // Step 1: Mesh-forwarded messages are always trusted  
    39→  if (senderAgentId === null) {  
    40→    return { allowed: true }  
    41→  }  
    42→  
    43→  // Load team membership for both parties  
    44→  const senderTeam = getClosedTeamForAgent(senderAgentId)  
    45→  const recipientTeam = getClosedTeamForAgent(recipientAgentId)  
    46→  
    47→  // Step 2: Neither party is in a closed team — open world, all  

... [2108 more chars truncated]  

</details>

     1→import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     2→import { checkMessageAllowed } from '@/lib/message-filter'  
     3→import { loadAgents } from '@/lib/agent-registry'  
     4→  
     5→// In-memory cache: avoids re-reading governance + teams files for every agent  
     6→// on each request. TTL of 5 seconds balances freshness with performance.  
     7→const cache = new Map<string, { ids: string[]; expiresAt: number }>()  
     8→const CACHE_TTL_MS = 5_000  
     9→  
    10→export async function GET(request: NextRequest) {  
    11→  try {  
    12→    const agentId = request.nextUrl.searchParams.get('agentId')  
    13→  
    14→    if (!agentId) {  
    15→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'agentId query parameter is required' }, { status: 400 })  
    16→    }  
    17→  
    18→    // Check cache first  
    19→    const cached = cache.get(agentId)  
    20→    if (cached && Date.now() < cached.expiresAt) {  
    21→      return NextResponse.json({ reachableAgentIds: cached.ids })  
    22→    }  
    23→  
    24→    // Cache miss or expired — compute reachable agents  
    25→    const allAgents = loadAgents()  
    26→    const reachableAgentIds: string[] = []  
    27→  
    28→    for (const agent of allAgents) {  
    29→      if (agent.id === agentId) continue  
    30→      if (agent.deletedAt) continue  
    31→  
    32→      const result = checkMessageAllowed({  
    33→        senderAgentId: agentId,  
    34→        recipientAgentId: agent.id,  
    35→      })  
    36→  
    37→      if (result.allowed) {  
    38→        reachableAgentIds.push(agent.id)  
    39→      }  
    40→    }  
    41→  
    42→    // Store in cache with TTL  
    43→    cache.set(agentId, { ids: reachableAgentIds, expiresAt: Date.now() + CACHE_TTL_MS })  
    44→  
    45→    // Evict stale entries to prevent unbounded growth  
    46→    if (cache.size > 200) {  
    47→      const now = Date.now()  
    48→      for (const [key, entry] of cache) {  
    49→        if (now >= entry.expiresAt) cache.delete(key)  
    50→      }  
    51  

... [286 more chars truncated]  

</details>

     1→/**  
     2→ * Team Resource ACL — checks whether an agent (or web UI request)  
     3→ * is allowed to access a given team's resources.  
     4→ *  
     5→ * Open teams (type undefined or 'open') impose no restrictions.  
     6→ * Closed teams restrict access to the manager, chief-of-staff,  
     7→ * and team members only.  
     8→ */  
     9→  
    10→import { isManager } from './governance'  
    11→import { getTeam } from './team-registry'  
    12→  
    13→export interface TeamAccessInput {  
    14→  teamId: string  
    15→  requestingAgentId?: string // undefined = web UI request (always allowed)  
    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface TeamAccessResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Determine whether the requester may access the team's resources.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Decision order:  
    27→ *  1. Web UI (no agentId)      → allowed  
    28→ *  2. Team not found           → allowed (caller handles 404)  
    29→ *  3. Team is open / untyped   → allowed  
    30→ *  4. Requester is MANAGER     → allowed  
    31→ *  5. Requester is chief-of-staff → allowed  
    32→ *  6. Requester is a member    → allowed  
    33→ *  7. Otherwise                → denied  
    34→ */  
    35→export function checkTeamAccess(input: TeamAccessInput): TeamAccessResult {  
    36→  // 1. Web UI requests (no X-Agent-Id header) always pass  
    37→  if (input.requestingAgentId === undefined) {  
    38→    return { allowed: true }  
    39→  }  
    40→  
    41→  // 2. Team not found — let the caller deal with 404  
    42→  const team = getTeam(input.teamId)  
    43→  if (!team) {  
    44→    return { allowed: true }  
    45→  }  
    46→  
    47→  // 3. Open teams (or teams with no explicit type) have no ACL  
    48→  if (team.type !== 'closed') {  
    49→    return { allowed: true }  
    50→  }  
    51→  
    52→  // 4. MANAGER role always has access  
    53→  if (isManager(input.requestingAgentId)) {  
    54→    return { allowed: true }  
    55→  }  
    56→  
    57→  // 5.   

... [466 more chars truncated]

     1→/**  
     2→ * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation  
     3→ *

     5→ * based on governance roles (MANAGER, Chief-of-Staff) and closed-team  
     6→ * membership. Open-world agents (not in any closed team) can message  
     7→ * freely unless the recipient is inside a closed team.  
     8→ */  
     9→  
    10→import { isManager, isChiefOfStaffAnywhere, getClosedTeamForAgent } from './governance'

    18→export interface MessageFilterResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Check whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Algorithm:  
    27→ * 1. Mesh-forwarded (senderAgentId null): always allowed (trust mesh peers)  
    28→ * 2. Neither in a closed team: allowed (open world, current behavior)  
    29→ * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed  
    30→ * 4. Sender is COS of any closed team: can reach MANAGER, other COS, own team members  
    31→ * 5. Normal closed-team member: can reach same-team members and own COS  
    32→ * 6. Outside sender to closed-team recipient: denied  
    33→ * 7. Default: allowed  
    34→ */  
    35→export function checkMessageAllowed(input: MessageFilterInput): MessageFilterResult {  
    36→  const { senderAgentId, recipientAgentId } = input  
    37→  
    38→  // Step 1: Mesh-forwarded messages are always trusted  
    39→  if (senderAgentId === null) {  
    40→    return { allowed: true }  
    41→  }  
    42→  
    43→  // Load team membership for both parties  
    44→  const senderTeam = getClosedTeamForAgent(senderAgentId)  
    45→  const recipientTeam = getClosedTeamForAgent(recipientAgentId)  
    46→  
    47→  // Step 2: Neither party is in a closed team — open world, all

   135→  const fromAgent = resolveAgentIdentifier(from)  
   136→

   138→  const isTargetLocal = !targetHostId || isSelf(targetHostId)  
   139→  
   140→  // Resolve recipient agent  
   141→  const toAgent = resolveAgentIdentifier(toIdentifier)  
   142→  
   143→  // For unresolved recipients, create minimal resolved info  
   144→  // NEVER use raw identifier as agentId - it could be a name  
   145→  const toResolved: ResolvedAgent = toAgent || {  
   146→    agentId: '',  // Empty string - forces UUID-based functions to resolve or fail  
   147→    alias: options.toAlias || toIdentifier,  
   148→    hostId: targetHostId || undefined,

   150→  }

     1→import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     2→import { checkMessageAllowed } from '@/lib/message-filter'  
     3→import { loadAgents } from '@/lib/agent-registry'  
     4→  
     5→// In-memory cache: avoids re-reading governance + teams files for every agent  
     6→// on each request. TTL of 5 seconds balances freshness with performance.  
     7→const cache = new Map<string, { ids: string[]; expiresAt: number }>()  
     8→const CACHE_TTL_MS = 5_000  
     9→  
    10→export async function GET(request: NextRequest) {  
    11→  try {  
    12→    const agentId = request.nextUrl.searchParams.get('agentId')  
    13→  
    14→    if (!agentId) {  
    15→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'agentId query parameter is required' }, { status: 400 })  
    16→    }  
    17→  
    18→    // Check cache first  
    19→    const cached = cache.get(agentId)  
    20→    if (cached && Date.now() < cached.expiresAt) {  
    21→      return NextResponse.json({ reachableAgentIds: cached.ids })  
    22→    }  
    23→  
    24→    // Cache miss or expired — compute reachable agents  
    25→    const allAgents = loadAgents()  
    26→    const reachableAgentIds: string[] = []  
    27→  
    28→    for (const agent of allAgents) {  
    29→      if (agent.id === agentId) continue  
    30→      if (agent.deletedAt) continue  
    31→  
    32→      const result = checkMessageAllowed({  
    33→        senderAgentId: agentId,  
    34→        recipientAgentId: agent.id,  
    35→      })  
    36→  
    37→      if (result.allowed) {  
    38→        reachableAgentIds.push(agent.id)  
    39→      }  
    40→    }  
    41→  
    42→    // Store in cache with TTL  
    43→    cache.set(agentId, { ids: reachableAgentIds, expiresAt: Date.now() + CACHE_TTL_MS })  
    44→  
    45→    // Evict stale entries to prevent unbounded growth  
    46→    if (cache.size > 200) {  
    47→      const now = Date.now()  
    48→      for (const [key, entry] of cache) {  
    49→        if (now >= entry.expiresAt) cache.delete(key)  
    50→      }  
    51  

... [286 more chars truncated]

     2→import { loadGovernance, setPassword, verifyPassword } from '@/lib/governance'  
     3→  
     4→export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
     5→  try {  
     6→    const body = await request.json()  
     7→    const { password, currentPassword } = body  
     8→  
     9→    if (!password || typeof password !== 'string' || password.length < 6) {  
    10→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Password must be at least 6 characters' }, { status: 400 })  
    11→    }  
    12→  
    13→    const config = loadGovernance()  
    14→  
    15→    // If password already set, require current password  
    16→    if (config.passwordHash) {  
    17→      if (!currentPassword || !verifyPassword(currentPassword)) {  
    18→        return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid current password' }, { status: 401 })  
    19→      }  
    20→    }  
    21→  
    22→    await setPassword(password)  
    23→    return NextResponse.json({ success: true })  
    24→  } catch (error) {  
    25→    console.error('Failed to set password:', error)  
    26→    return NextResponse.json(  
    27→      { error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Failed to set password' },  
    28→      { status: 500 }  
    29→    )  
    30→  }  
    31→}
